   191→/** Convert an AMP envelope-format message to internal Message format */
   192→function convertAMPToMessage(ampMsg: any): Message | null {
   193→  const envelope = ampMsg.envelope
   194→  const payload = ampMsg.payload
   195→  if (!envelope || !payload) return null
   196→
   197→  // Validate required envelope fields individually (defense-in-depth against malformed AMP messages)
   198→  if (!envelope.id || !envelope.from || !envelope.to || !envelope.subject) {
   199→    console.warn('[MessageQueue] Skipping message with missing required envelope fields:', {
   200→      id: envelope.id || 'unknown',
   201→      hasId: !!envelope.id,
   202→      hasFrom: !!envelope.from,
   203→      hasTo: !!envelope.to,
   204→      hasSubject: !!envelope.subject,
   205→    })
   206→    return null
   207→  }

   209→  const fromName = extractAgentNameFromAddress(envelope.from)
   210→  const toName = extractAgentNameFromAddress(envelope.to)

   212→  const toHost = extractHostFromAddress(envelope.to)

   214→  const status = ampMsg.metadata?.status || ampMsg.local?.status || 'unread'

   594→/**
   595→ * Kill all tmux sessions belonging to an agent.
   596→ * Extracted from deleteAgent() so it can be reused by both soft-delete and hard-delete paths.
   597→ */
   598→function killAgentSessions(agent: Agent): void {
   599→  const agentName = agent.name || agent.alias
   600→  if (!agentName) return
   601→
   602→  const { execSync } = require('child_process')
   603→
   604→  // Kill sessions for all indices in the sessions array
   605→  const sessions = agent.sessions || []
   606→  for (const session of sessions) {
   607→    const sessionName = computeSessionName(agentName, session.index)
   608→    try {
   609→      execSync(`tmux kill-session -t "${sessionName}" 2>/dev/null || true`, { encoding: 'utf-8' })
   610→      console.log(`[Agent Registry] Killed tmux session: ${sessionName}`)
   611→    } catch (error) {
   612→      console.log(`[Agent Registry] Could not kill tmux session ${sessionName} (may not exist)`)
   613→    }
   614→  }
   615→
   616→  // Also try to kill the base session name (in case sessions array is empty)
   617→  if (sessions.length === 0) {
   618→    try {
   619→      execSync(`tmux kill-session -t "${agentName}" 2>/dev/null || true`, { encoding: 'utf-8' })
   620→      console.log(`[Agent Registry] Killed tmux session: ${agentName}`)
   621→    } catch (error) {
   622→      console.log(`[Agent Registry] Could not kill tmux session ${agentName} (may not exist)`)
   623→    }
   624→  }
   625→}

   193→    const resizeObserver = new ResizeObserver(() => {

   199→    // Add keyboard shortcuts for scrolling, copy, and paste
   200→    terminal.attachCustomKeyEventHandler((event) => {
   201→      // Calculate scroll amount based on terminal height (scroll by page)
   202→      const scrollAmount = Math.max(1, terminal.rows - 2)
   203→
   204→      // Shift + Page Up - Scroll up by page
   205→      if (event.shiftKey && event.key === 'PageUp') {
   206→        terminal.scrollLines(-scrollAmount)
   207→        return false
   208→      }
   209→      // Shift + Page Down - Scroll down by page
   210→      if (event.shiftKey && event.key === 'PageDown') {
   211→        terminal.scrollLines(scrollAmount)
   212→        return false
   213→      }
   214→      // Shift + Arrow Up - Scroll up 5 lines
   215→      if (event.shiftKey && event.key === 'ArrowUp') {
   216→        terminal.scrollLines(-5)
   217→        return false
   218→      }

   345→// STREAMING LINE COUNTER (avoids loading entire file into memory)
   346→// ============================================================================
   347→function countFileLines(filePath: string): number {
   348→  const buffer = Buffer.alloc(64 * 1024) // 64KB read buffer
   349→  const fd = fs.openSync(filePath, 'r')
   350→  let count = 0
   351→  let bytesRead: number
   352→  let leftover = ''
   353→
   354→  try {
   355→    while ((bytesRead = fs.readSync(fd, buffer, 0, buffer.length, null)) > 0) {
   356→      const chunk = leftover + buffer.toString('utf-8', 0, bytesRead)
   357→      const lines = chunk.split('\n')
   358→      leftover = lines.pop() || ''
   359→      for (const line of lines) {
   360→        if (line.trim()) count++
   361→      }
   362→    }
   363→    if (leftover.trim()) count++
   364→  } finally {
   365→    fs.closeSync(fd)
   366→  }
   367→  return count
   368→}
   369→

   371→// MAIN ENTRY: runIndexDelta — callable directly (no HTTP)

   374→  success: boolean

   418→// In-memory cache for resolved agent addresses (avoids expensive 8-step resolution on every call).
   419→// Entries expire after AGENT_CACHE_TTL_MS. Primary use case: when a message arrives from an external
   420→// agent, the sender's address is cached so that replies route back without re-resolving.
   421→const AGENT_CACHE_TTL_MS = 5 * 60 * 1000 // 5 minutes
   422→const agentAddressCache = new Map<string, { resolved: ResolvedAgent; resolvedAt: number }>()
   423→
   424→// Proactive cache sweep every 5 minutes to prevent unbounded memory growth
   425→setInterval(() => {
   426→  const now = Date.now()
   427→  for (const [key, entry] of agentAddressCache) {
   428→    if (now - entry.resolvedAt > AGENT_CACHE_TTL_MS) {
   429→      agentAddressCache.delete(key)
   430→    }
   431→  }

   439→ *   - "name" → resolve on self host, then any host
   440→ *   - "session_name" → parse and resolve
   441→ *
   442→ * Results are cached in-memory for 5 minutes to speed up reply routing.

    60→ */
    61→async function sendTmuxNotification(sessionName: string, message: string): Promise<void> {
    62→  // Escape single quotes in the message
    63→  const escapedMessage = message.replace(/'/g, "'\\''")
    64→
    65→  // Target the first pane of the first window
    66→  const target = `${sessionName}:0.0`
    67→
    68→  // Send text and Enter atomically via tmux \; command chaining to prevent race conditions
    69→  // Uses -l (literal) flag to prevent tmux from misinterpreting key names in notification text
    70→  // Note: If the session is running a non-shell program (vim, REPL, TUI), this echo command
    71→  // will be typed as input to that program. Notifications are designed for idle shell prompts.
    72→  await execAsync(`tmux send-keys -t "${target}" -l "echo '${escapedMessage}'" \\; send-keys -t "${target}" Enter`)
    73→}

## <span style="color:#4CAF50">◇ ASSISTANT</span>  *[2026-02-15 20:16:08]*

Yes, this is a circular dependency:
- `agent-registry.ts` imports `invalidateAgentCache` from `messageQueue.ts`
- `messageQueue.ts` imports `getAgentBySession, getAgentByName, ...` from `agent-registry.ts`

In Node.js/TypeScript with module resolution, this can work at runtime because by the time the functions are called, both modules are fully loaded. The import happens at module-level, but the functions are only called later. However, this is an architectural concern. Let me check if this circular dependency could cause issues specifically with CommonJS or ESM resolution.

## <span style="color:#4CAF50">◇ ASSISTANT</span>  *[2026-02-15 20:16:15]*

With Next.js using bundler module resolution and ESM, circular dependencies between modules work fine at runtime as long as neither module tries to access a value from the other at the top level (during initialization). In this case, `agent-registry.ts` imports `invalidateAgentCache` (a function) and only calls it inside other function bodies, not at module load time. Similarly, `messageQueue.ts` imports functions from `agent-registry.ts` and only calls them inside function bodies. This is safe.

    19→ */
    20→export function escapeForCozo(s: string | undefined | null): string {
    21→  if (!s) return 'null'
    22→
    23→  return "'" + s
    24→    .replace(/\\/g, '\\\\')   // Escape backslashes first (order matters!)
    25→    .replace(/'/g, "\\'")     // Then escape single quotes
    26→    .replace(/\n/g, '\\n')    // Then escape newlines
    27→    .replace(/\r/g, '\\r')    // Then escape carriage returns
    28→    .replace(/\t/g, '\\t')    // Then escape tabs
    29→    + "'"
    30→}
    31→
    32→/**
    33→ * Escape a string but return without quotes (for building complex expressions)
    34→ *
    35→ * @param s - The string to escape
    36→ * @returns Escaped string WITHOUT surrounding quotes
    37→ */
    38→export function escapeForCozoRaw(s: string): string {
    39→  return s
    40→    .replace(/\\/g, '\\\\')
    41→    .replace(/'/g, "\\'")
    42→    .replace(/\n/g, '\\n')
    43→    .replace(/\r/g, '\\r')
    44→    .replace(/\t/g, '\\t')

</details>

## <span style="color:#4CAF50">◇ ASSISTANT</span>  *[2026-02-15 20:17:58]*

One thing to note: `escapeForCozo` handles `null`/`undefined` by returning the string `'null'` (without quotes). In the consolidate.ts code, the `agentId` and `memoryId` parameters are typed as `string`, so they should never be null/undefined. This is safe.

Let me also verify there's no issue with the `Cmd+C` / `Ctrl+C` handler -- specifically, on macOS, `Cmd+C` checks `event.metaKey && event.key === 'c'`. When there's no selection, this should fall through to `return true` which passes the event to the terminal. But wait - on macOS, `Cmd+C` would be the copy shortcut, not `Ctrl+C` for SIGINT. The terminal PTY would receive `Ctrl+C` as the interrupt, not `Cmd+C`. So the fallthrough behavior makes sense: if user presses `Cmd+C` with no selection, it just passes through harmlessly (the terminal won't interpret `Cmd+C` as SIGINT because that's `Ctrl+C`).

Actually, let me re-read the code more carefully.

   235→      // Cmd+C (macOS) or Ctrl+Shift+C (Linux) - Copy selection to clipboard
   236→      // When there IS a selection, copy it; when there is NO selection, let Ctrl+C pass through as interrupt
   237→      if ((event.metaKey && event.key === 'c') || (event.ctrlKey && event.shiftKey && event.key === 'C')) {
   238→        if (event.type === 'keydown') {
   239→          const selection = terminal.getSelection()
   240→          if (selection) {
   241→            navigator.clipboard.writeText(selection).catch((err) => {
   242→              // Clipboard failed but user had a selection, so copy was the intent - no SIGINT needed
   243→              console.warn('[Terminal] Failed to copy selection:', err)
   244→            })
   245→            return false // Prevent sending Ctrl+C interrupt to PTY (copy was intent since selection existed)
   246→          }
   247→          // No selection: fall through to let Ctrl+C pass as SIGINT (return true at end of handler)
   248→        }
   249→      }
   250→
   251→      // Cmd+V (macOS) or Ctrl+Shift+V (Linux) - Paste from clipboard into PTY via WebSocket
   252→      if ((event.metaKey && event.key === 'v') || (event.ctrlKey && event.shiftKey && event.key === 'V')) {
   253→        if (event.type === 'keydown') {
   254→          navigator.clipboard.readText().then((text) => {

</details>


## <span style="color:#4CAF50">◇ ASSISTANT</span>  *[2026-02-15 20:18:06]*

The comment says "let Ctrl+C pass through as SIGINT" but the condition is for `Cmd+C` (macOS) or `Ctrl+Shift+C` (Linux). On macOS, when there's no selection and the user presses `Cmd+C`, returning `true` will pass the event to xterm.js, which by default handles `Cmd+C` as... actually xterm.js doesn't map `Cmd+C` to SIGINT. Only `Ctrl+C` maps to SIGINT in terminal. So the comment is slightly misleading -- on macOS, `Cmd+C` without selection just does nothing (passes through to terminal which ignores it). On Linux, `Ctrl+Shift+C` without selection would similarly just pass through.

This is a minor comment inaccuracy but the behavior is functionally correct. The important thing is that `Cmd+C` with selection copies, and without selection it doesn't interfere. Plain `Ctrl+C` (without meta/shift) is never intercepted by this handler, so SIGINT always works.

Now I have all the information needed. Let me write the comprehensive audit report.

---

# Audit Report: PR #216 - fix(install): quote variables to prevent word-splitting

**Generated:** 2026-02-15
**Reviewer:** judge-agent
**Issue:** #211
**PR:** #216

## Verdict: APPROVED

## Summary

**Goal:** Quote two unquoted variable expansions in `install.sh` to prevent word-splitting and globbing (ShellCheck SC2086).
**Goal Achieved:** Yes
**Behavior Preserved:** Yes -- quoting these variables makes them safer without changing semantics.

## Diff Analysis

The PR contains exactly 2 changes in `install.sh`, both correct:

### Change 1: Line 293 (diff hunk @@ -281,7 +281,7 @@)

**Before:**
```bash
NODE_MAJOR=$(echo $NODE_VERSION | cut -d'.' -f1 | sed 's/v//')
```
**After:**
```bash
NODE_MAJOR=$(echo "$NODE_VERSION" | cut -d'.' -f1 | sed 's/v//')
```

**Analysis:** CORRECT. `$NODE_VERSION` contains output of `node --version` (e.g., `v20.11.0`). While this value will never contain spaces or glob characters in practice, quoting it is the correct defensive practice. The quoting does not change behavior for any valid node version string. Without quotes, if `NODE_VERSION` were empty, `echo` would output a blank line and `cut` would still work, so behavior is identical either way.

### Change 2: Line 997 (diff hunk @@ -979,7 +979,7 @@)

**Before:**
```bash
echo "   cd $INSTALL_DIR"
```
**After:**
```bash
echo "   cd \"$INSTALL_DIR\""
```

**Analysis:** CORRECT and IMPORTANT. This is inside a double-quoted `echo` so the `$INSTALL_DIR` was already protected from word-splitting by the outer quotes. However, the fix adds escaped inner quotes around the path in the _output_, which means users who copy-paste the displayed command will get `cd "/path/to/ai-maestro"` instead of `cd /path/to/ai-maestro`. This is a UX improvement -- if a user installs to a path with spaces, the displayed command will now work correctly when copy-pasted.

### No Other Changes

Confirmed: The diff contains exactly 2 hunks, each changing exactly 1 line. No other files are modified.

## Behavior Preservation

| Aspect | Before | After | Preserved? |
|--------|--------|-------|------------|
| Node version parsing | Works for all valid version strings | Identical | Yes |
| `cd` instruction display | Shows unquoted path | Shows quoted path | Yes (improved) |
| Script exit codes | Unchanged | Unchanged | Yes |
| Script flow | Unch

## <span style="color:#4CAF50">◇ ASSISTANT</span>  *[2026-02-15 20:16:06]*

This is important. The UI components use `fromLabel` and `toLabel` with fallback chains: `fromLabel || fromAlias || from`. So when `fromLabel` is undefined (the bug), the UI falls back to `fromAlias` (which IS populated). The user-visible impact is that display labels are missing, but aliases are shown instead. The fix is correct in intent.

Now let me also note that the UI uses `(msg as any).fromLabel` -- the `as any` cast suggests the MessageSummary type might not directly expose these fields in the component's type definition, or there's a type mismatch. But the MessageSummary interface (line 74) does define `fromLabel?: string`, so the `as any` is unnecessary. That's a pre-existing issue, not from this PR.

Now I'll write the report.

# PR #213 Audit Report
Generated: 2026-02-15
Reviewer: judge-agent

## Summary
**NEEDS WORK** - The fix in `convertAMPToMessage()` is correct and well-implemented, but there is a secondary propagation gap: the AMP summary builder (lines 296-309) does not copy `fromLabel`/`toLabel` from the converted Message to the MessageSummary, so list views will still lack labels.

## Verification Checklist

### 1. Imports -- PASS
Both `getAgentByName` and `getAgentByAlias` are already imported at line 6 of `lib/messageQueue.ts` from `./agent-registry`. No new imports needed.

### 2. Function Signatures -- PASS
- `getAgentByName(name: string, hostId?: string): Agent | null` (line 228, agent-registry.ts)
- `getAgentByAlias(alias: string, hostId?: string): Agent | null` (line 267, agent-registry.ts)
- Both return `Agent | null`, and the `Agent` interface has `label?: string` (line 156, types/agent.ts)

### 3. convertAMPToMessage Fix -- PASS
The fix correctly:
- Resolves agents via `getAgentByName(fromName) || getAgentByAlias(fromName)` (tries name first, then alias)
- Falls back to raw name if agent not found: `fromAgent?.label || fromName`
- Adds `fromLabel` and `toLabel` to the returned Message object
- Placement is correct (after name extraction, before return)

### 4. Fallback Behavior -- PASS
- If agent not found in registry, `fromAgent` is null, so `fromAgent?.label` is undefined, and `fromLabel` becomes `fromName` (the raw extracted name). This is correct.
- If agent found but has no label, `agent.label` is undefined, so falls back to `fromName`. Correct.

### 5. Type Correctness -- PASS
- `Message.fromLabel?: string` (line 27) and `Message.toLabel?: string` (line 33) are properly typed
- `MessageSummary.fromLabel?: string` (line 74) and `MessageSummary.toLabel?: string` (line 79) are properly typed

### 6. No Regressions to Existing Logic -- PASS
The diff only adds new lines; no existing lines are modified or removed. The new code is inserted between the `status` assignment and the `return` statement. All existing fields in the return object are untouched.

## <span style="color:#4CAF50">◇ ASSISTANT</span>  *[2026-02-15 20:16:17]*

Important finding: `writeToAMPSent` does NOT store `sender_public_key` at the top level (unlike `writeToAMPInbox`). This means for sent messages viewed via `getMessage(agent, id, 'sent')`, the `amp` object will only have `signature`, `ampAddress`, and `envelopeId` but NOT `senderPublicKey`. This is a minor note but not a bug -- sent messages wouldn't have an external sender's key. The sender already knows their own key.

---

# Refactoring Review: PR #214 - fix(amp): preserve signature verification data in convertAMPToMessage

Generated: 2026-02-15
Reviewer: judge-agent
Issue: #208

## Verdict: APPROVED (with one advisory note)

## Summary

**Refactoring Goal:** Populate the `amp` field on `Message` objects returned by `convertAMPToMessage()` so that cryptographic verification data (signature, sender public key, AMP address, envelope ID) is not discarded during conversion.

**Goal Achieved:** Yes

**Behavior Preserved:** Yes -- no existing fields are modified; only the previously-undefined `amp` field is now populated.

## Quality Metrics

| Metric | Before | After | Verdict |
|--------|--------|-------|---------|
| Lines of Code (convertAMPToMessage) | 43 | 53 | +10 lines, acceptable |
| Missing interface fields | `amp` always undefined | `amp` populated when data exists | Fixed |
| Data loss | Signature/key discarded | Signature/key preserved | Fixed |

## Behavior Analysis

### Preserved Behaviors

- [X] `convertAMPToMessage` still returns `null` for missing envelope/payload
- [X] `convertAMPToMessage` still validates required envelope fields (id, from, to, subject)
- [X] All existing fields (id, from, fromAlias, fromHost, to, toAlias, toHost, timestamp, subject, priority, status, content, inReplyTo) are unchanged
- [X] `collectMessagesFromAMPDir` (creates `MessageSummary`, not `Message`) is unaffected
- [X] `getMessage()` callers now get richer data but no breaking changes

### Changed Behaviors

| Behavior | Before | After | Acceptable? |
|----------|--------|-------|-------------|
| `message.amp` | Always `undefined` | Object with signature data (or `undefined` if no sig/key) | Yes -- additive only |

## Data Flow Trace (VERIFIED)

### Write Path: `writeToAMPInbox()` (lib/amp-inbox-writer.ts:307-369)

Stores JSON with this structure:
```json
{
  "envelope": {
    "signature": "base64-string-or-null"   // line 340
  },
```

## <span style="color:#4CAF50">◇ ASSISTANT</span>  *[2026-02-15 20:14:58]*

This is a significant finding. The `install-hooks.sh` script does NOT accept `-y` at all. It has no argument parsing. Passing `-y` will be silently ignored by bash (since the script doesn't use `$1` or `$@` or `getopts`), so it won't break anything -- but it also won't change behavior. However, the script itself doesn't have any interactive prompts either (no `read` commands). So the original bug report might be inaccurate about this specific script blocking.

Let me verify there are truly no interactive prompts in the full script.
